			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">World Health Organization</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

<p>The <b>World Health Organization</b> (<b>WHO</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agency of the United Nations</a> that is concerned with international <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>. It was established on 7 April 1948, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, Switzerland. The WHO is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Group" title="United Nations Development Group">United Nations Development Group</a>. Its predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_Health_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="League of Nations Health Organization">Health Organization</a>, was an agency of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>.</p>
<p>The constitution of the World Health Organization had been signed by 61 countries on 22 July 1946, with the first meeting of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a> finishing on 24 July 1948. It incorporated the <i>Office international d'hygiène publique</i> and the League of Nations Health Organization. Since its creation, it has played a leading role in the <a href="/wiki/Eradication_of_infectious_diseases" title="Eradication of infectious diseases">eradication</a> of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>. Its current priorities include <a href="/wiki/Communicable_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Communicable disease">communicable diseases</a>, in particular <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebola" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola">Ebola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>; the mitigation of the effects of non-communicable diseases; sexual and reproductive health, development, and aging; nutrition, food security and healthy eating; occupational health; substance abuse; and driving the development of reporting, publications, and networking.</p>
<p>The WHO is responsible for the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Report" title="World Health Report">World Health Report</a>, a leading international publication on health, the worldwide World Health Survey, and <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Day" title="World Health Day">World Health Day</a> (7 April of every year). The head of WHO is <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Chan" title="Margaret Chan">Margaret Chan</a>.</p>
<p>The 2014/2015 proposed budget of the WHO is about US$4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Fin2013_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fin2013-1">[1]</a></sup> About US$930 million are to be provided by member states with a further US$3 billion to be from voluntary contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-Fin2013_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fin2013-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment">Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 1945 United Nations Conference on International Organization, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Szeming_Sze" title="Szeming Sze">Szeming Sze</a>, a delegate from China, conferred with Norwegian and Brazilian delegates on creating an international health organization under the auspices of the new United Nations. After failing to get a resolution passed on the subject, <a href="/wiki/Alger_Hiss" title="Alger Hiss">Alger Hiss</a>, the Secretary General of the conference, recommended using a declaration to establish such an organization. Dr. Sze and other delegates lobbied and a declaration passed calling for an international conference on health.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_ULS_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_ULS-2">[2]</a></sup> The use of the word "world", rather than "international", emphasized the truly global nature of what the organization was seeking to achieve.<sup id="cite_ref-bmj1948_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmj1948-3">[3]</a></sup> The constitution of the World Health Organization was signed by all 51 countries of the United Nations, and by 10 other countries, on 22 July 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle_1947_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle_1947-4">[4]</a></sup> It thus became the first specialised agency of the United Nations to which every member subscribed.<sup id="cite_ref-shimkin_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shimkin-5">[5]</a></sup> Its constitution formally came into force on the first <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Day" title="World Health Day">World Health Day</a> on 7 April 1948, when it was ratified by the 26th member state.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle_1947_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle_1947-4">[4]</a></sup> The first meeting of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a> finished on 24 July 1948, having secured a budget of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$5 million</span> (then <span style="white-space: nowrap">GB£1,250,000</span>) for the 1949 year. <a href="/wiki/Andrija_Stampar" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrija Stampar">Andrija Stampar</a> was the Assembly's first president, and <a href="/wiki/G._Brock_Chisholm" class="mw-redirect" title="G. Brock Chisholm">G. Brock Chisholm</a> was appointed Director-General of WHO, having served as Executive Secretary during the planning stages.<sup id="cite_ref-bmj1948_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmj1948-3">[3]</a></sup> Its first priorities were to control the spread of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infection" title="Sexually transmitted infection">sexually transmitted infections</a>, and to improve <a href="/wiki/Maternal_health" title="Maternal health">maternal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Child_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Child health">child health</a>, nutrition and environmental hygiene. Its first legislative act was concerning the compilation of accurate statistics on the spread and morbidity of disease.<sup id="cite_ref-bmj1948_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmj1948-3">[3]</a></sup> The logo of the World Health Organization features the <a href="/wiki/Rod_of_Asclepius" title="Rod of Asclepius">Rod of Asclepius</a> as a symbol for healing.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">Operational history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operational history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/220px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/330px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg/440px-Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2220" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Directors_of_Global_Smallpox_Eradication_Program.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Three former directors of the <a href="/wiki/Smallpox#Eradication" title="Smallpox">Global Smallpox Eradication Programme</a> read the news that smallpox had been globally eradicated, 1980</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>IT established an epidemiological information service via <a href="/wiki/Telex" title="Telex">telex</a> in 1947, and by 1950 a mass <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> inoculation drive (using the <a href="/wiki/BCG_vaccine" title="BCG vaccine">BCG vaccine</a>) was under way. In 1955, the malaria eradication programme was launched, although it was later altered in objective. 1965 saw the first report on <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes mellitus</a> and the creation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Agency_for_Research_on_Cancer" title="International Agency for Research on Cancer">International Agency for Research on Cancer</a>. WHO moved into its headquarters building in 1966. The <a href="/wiki/Expanded_Programme_on_Immunization" class="mw-redirect" title="Expanded Programme on Immunization">Expanded Programme on Immunization</a> was started in 1974, as was the control programme into <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">onchocerciasis</a> – an important partnership between the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP), and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>. In the following year, the Special Programme for Research and Training in Tropical Diseases was also launched. In 1976, the World Health Assembly voted to enact a resolution on Disability Prevention and Rehabilitation, with a focus on community-driven care. The first list of <a href="/wiki/Essential_medicines" title="Essential medicines">essential medicines</a> was drawn up in 1977, and a year later the ambitious goal of "health for all" was declared. In 1986, WHO started its global programme on the growing problem of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, followed two years later by additional attention on preventing discrimination against sufferers and <a href="/wiki/UNAIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a> was formed in 1996. The <a href="/wiki/Global_Polio_Eradication_Initiative" title="Global Polio Eradication Initiative">Global Polio Eradication Initiative</a> was established in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-at60_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at60-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1958, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Zhdanov" title="Viktor Zhdanov">Viktor Zhdanov</a>, Deputy Minister of Health for the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a>, called on the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a> to undertake a global initiative to <a href="/wiki/Eradication_of_infectious_diseases" title="Eradication of infectious diseases">eradicate</a> smallpox, resulting in Resolution WHA11.54.<sup id="cite_ref-Fenner2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fenner2-8">[8]</a></sup> At this point, 2 million people were dying from smallpox every year. In 1967, the World Health Organization intensified the global smallpox eradication by contributing $2.4 million annually to the effort and adopted a new <a href="/wiki/Disease_surveillance" title="Disease surveillance">disease surveillance</a> method.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The initial problem the WHO team faced was inadequate reporting of smallpox cases. WHO established a network of consultants who assisted countries in setting up surveillance and containment activities.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The WHO also helped contain the last European outbreak in <a href="/wiki/1972_outbreak_of_smallpox_in_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="1972 outbreak of smallpox in Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia in 1972</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> After over two decades of fighting <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, the WHO declared in 1979 that the disease had been eradicated – the first disease in history to be eliminated by human effort.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, WHO's Director General highlighted gains in child survival, reduced <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a>, increased life expectancy and reduced rates of "scourges" such as smallpox and <a href="/wiki/Polio" class="mw-redirect" title="Polio">polio</a> on the fiftieth anniversary of WHO's founding. He, did, however, accept that more had to be done to assist maternal health and that progress in this area had been slow.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">Cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> have remained problems since WHO's founding, although in decline for a large part of that period.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In the twenty-first century, the <a href="/wiki/Stop_TB_Partnership" title="Stop TB Partnership">Stop TB Partnership</a> was created in 2000, along with the UN's formulation of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">Measles</a> initiative was formed in 2001, and credited with reducing global deaths from the disease by 68% by 2007. In 2002, <a href="/wiki/The_Global_Fund_to_Fight_AIDS,_Tuberculosis_and_Malaria" title="The Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria">The Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria</a> was drawn up to improve the resources available.<sup id="cite_ref-at60_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at60-7">[7]</a></sup> In 2006, the organization endorsed the world's first official HIV/AIDS Toolkit for Zimbabwe, which formed the basis for a global prevention, treatment and support plan to fight the <a href="/wiki/AIDS_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="AIDS pandemic">AIDS pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_focus">Overall focus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Overall focus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WHO's Constitution states that its objective "is the attainment by all people of the highest possible level of health".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO fulfills its objective through its functions as defined in its Constitution: (a) to act as the directing and co-ordinating authority on international health work (b) to establish and maintain effective collaboration with the United Nations, specialized agencies, governmental health administrations, professional groups and such other organizations as may be deemed appropriate (c) to assist Governments, upon request, in strengthening health services (d) to furnish appropriate technical assistance and, in emergencies, necessary aid upon the request or acceptance of Governments (e) to provide or assist in providing, upon the request of the United Nations, health services and facilities to special groups, such as the peoples of trust territories (f) to establish and maintain such administrative and technical services as may be required, including epidemiological and statistical services (g) to stimulate and advance work to eradicate epidemic, endemic and other diseases (h) to promote, in co-operation with other specialized agencies where necessary, the prevention of accidental injuries (i) to promote, in co-operation with other specialized agencies where necessary, the improvement of nutrition, housing, sanitation, recreation, economic or working conditions and other aspects of environmental hygiene (j) to promote co-operation among scientific and professional groups which contribute to the advancement of health (k) to propose conventions, agreements and regulations, and make recommendations with respect to international health matters and to perform.</p>
<p>WHO currently defines its role in public health as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>providing leadership on matters critical to health and engaging in partnerships where joint action is needed;</li>
<li>shaping the research agenda and stimulating the generation, translation and dissemination of valuable knowledge;<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>setting norms and standards and promoting and monitoring their implementation;</li>
<li>articulating ethical and evidence-based policy options;</li>
<li>providing technical support, catalyzing change, and building sustainable institutional capacity; and</li>
<li>monitoring the health situation and assessing health trends.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communicable_diseases">Communicable diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Communicable diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2012–2013 WHO budget identified 5 areas among which funding was distributed.<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup> Two of those five areas related to <a href="/wiki/Communicable_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Communicable diseases">communicable diseases</a>: the first, to reduce the "health, social and economic burden" of communicable diseases in general; the second to combat <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a>, WHO works within the <a href="/wiki/UNAIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAIDS">UNAIDS</a> network and considers it important that it works in alignment with UNAIDS objectives and strategies. It also strives to involve sections of society other than health to help deal with the economic and social effects of the disease.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In line with UNAIDS, WHO has set itself the interim task between 2009 and 2015 of reducing the number of those aged 15–24 years who are infected by 50%; reducing new HIV infections in children by 90%; and reducing HIV-related deaths by 25%.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although WHO dropped its commitment to a global malaria eradication campaign in the 1970s as too ambitious, it retains a strong commitment to malaria control. WHO's Global Malaria Programme works to keep track of malaria cases, and future problems in malaria control schemes. WHO is to report, likely in 2015, as to whether <a href="/wiki/RTS,S" title="RTS,S">RTS,S</a>/AS01, currently in research, is a viable <a href="/wiki/Malaria_vaccine" title="Malaria vaccine">malaria vaccine</a>. For the time being, <a href="/wiki/Insecticide" title="Insecticide">insecticide</a>-treated <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_net" title="Mosquito net">mosquito nets</a> and insecticide sprays are used to prevent the spread of malaria, as are <a href="/wiki/Antimalarial_drugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Antimalarial drugs">antimalarial drugs</a> – particularly to vulnerable people such as pregnant women and young children.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO's help has contributed to a 40% fall in the number of deaths from <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> between 1990 and 2010, and since 2005, it claims that over 46 million people have been treated and an estimated 7 million lives saved through practices advocated by WHO. These include engaging national governments and their financing, early diagnosis, standardising treatment, monitoring of the spread and impact of tuberculosis and stabilising the drug supply. It has also recognised the vulnerability of victims of HIV/AIDS to tuberculosis.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO aims to eradicate <a href="/wiki/Polio" class="mw-redirect" title="Polio">polio</a>. It has also been successful in helping to reduce cases by 99% since the Global Polio Eradication Initiative was launched in 1988, which partnered WHO with <a href="/wiki/Rotary_International" title="Rotary International">Rotary International</a>, the <a href="/wiki/US_Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" class="mw-redirect" title="US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Children%27s_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Children's Fund">United Nations Children's Fund</a> (UNICEF), as well as smaller organizations. It works to immunize young children and prevent the re-emergence of cases in countries declared "polio-free".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-communicable_diseases">Non-communicable diseases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Non-communicable diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another of the thirteen WHO priority areas is aimed at the prevention and reduction of "disease, disability and premature deaths from chronic <a href="/wiki/Noncommunicable_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Noncommunicable disease">noncommunicable diseases</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">mental disorders</a>, violence and <a href="/wiki/Injury_prevention" title="Injury prevention">injuries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Visual_impairment" title="Visual impairment">visual impairment</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_health">Environmental health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Environmental health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WHO estimates that 12.6 million people died as a result of living or working in an unhealthy environment in 2012 – this accounts for nearly 1 in 4 of total global deaths. Environmental risk factors, such as air, water and soil pollution, chemical exposures, climate change, and ultraviolet radiation, contribute to more than 100 diseases and injuries. This can result in a number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_pollution-related_diseases" title="List of pollution-related diseases">pollution-related diseases</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_course_and_life_style">Life course and life style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Life course and life style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>WHO works to "reduce <a href="/wiki/Morbidity" class="mw-redirect" title="Morbidity">morbidity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">mortality</a> and improve health during key stages of life, including pregnancy, childbirth, the <a href="/wiki/Infant" title="Infant">neonatal period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Childhood" title="Childhood">childhood</a> and adolescence, and improve <a href="/wiki/Sexual_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual health">sexual</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">reproductive health</a> and promote active and healthy aging for all individuals".<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>It also tries to prevent or reduce risk factors for "health conditions associated with use of tobacco, alcohol, <a href="/wiki/Drugs" class="mw-redirect" title="Drugs">drugs</a> and other psychoactive substances, unhealthy diets and physical inactivity and <a href="/wiki/Unsafe_sex" class="mw-redirect" title="Unsafe sex">unsafe sex</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO works to improve nutrition, <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">food safety</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a> and to ensure this has a positive effect on <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surgery_and_trauma_care">Surgery and trauma care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Surgery and trauma care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WHO promotes road safety as a means to reduce traffic-related injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO has also worked on global initiatives in surgery, including emergency and essential surgical care,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> trauma care,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and safe surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/WHO_Surgical_Safety_Checklist" title="WHO Surgical Safety Checklist">WHO Surgical Safety Checklist</a> is in current use worldwide in the effort to improve patient safety.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_work">Emergency work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Emergency work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The World Health Organization's primary objective in natural and man-made emergencies is to coordinate with Member States and other stakeholders to "reduce avoidable loss of life and the burden of disease and disability."<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 May 2014, WHO announced that the spread of <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a> is a world health emergency – outbreaks of the disease in Asia, Africa and the Middle East are considered "extraordinary".<sup id="cite_ref-AP-20140505_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20140505-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20140505_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140505-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 August 2014, WHO declared that the spread of <a href="/wiki/Ebola" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola">Ebola</a> is a public health emergency; an outbreak which is believed to have started in <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, has spread to other nearby countries such as <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>. The situation in West Africa is considered very serious.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_policy">Health policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Health policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>WHO addresses government <a href="/wiki/Health_policy" title="Health policy">health policy</a> with two aims: firstly, "to address the underlying social and economic determinants of health through policies and programmes that enhance health equity and integrate pro-poor, gender-responsive, and human rights-based approaches" and secondly "to promote a healthier environment, intensify primary prevention and influence public policies in all sectors so as to address the root causes of environmental threats to health".<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The organization develops and promotes the use of evidence-based tools, norms and standards to support member states to inform <a href="/wiki/Health_policy" title="Health policy">health policy</a> options. It oversees the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Health_Regulations" title="International Health Regulations">International Health Regulations</a>, and publishes a series of <a href="/wiki/Medical_classification" title="Medical classification">medical classifications</a>; of these, three are overreaching "reference classifications": the <a href="/wiki/International_Statistical_Classification_of_Diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="International Statistical Classification of Diseases">International Statistical Classification of Diseases</a> (ICD), the <a href="/wiki/International_Classification_of_Functioning,_Disability_and_Health" title="International Classification of Functioning, Disability and Health">International Classification of Functioning, Disability and Health</a> (ICF) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Classification_of_Health_Interventions" title="International Classification of Health Interventions">International Classification of Health Interventions</a> (ICHI).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Other international policy frameworks produced by WHO include the <a href="/wiki/International_Code_of_Marketing_of_Breast-milk_Substitutes" title="International Code of Marketing of Breast-milk Substitutes">International Code of Marketing of Breast-milk Substitutes</a> (adopted in 1981),<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_on_Tobacco_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Framework Convention on Tobacco Control">Framework Convention on Tobacco Control</a> (adopted in 2003)<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Health_Human_Resources#Global_Code_of_Practice_on_the_International_Recruitment_of_Health_Personnel" class="mw-redirect" title="Health Human Resources">Global Code of Practice on the International Recruitment of Health Personnel</a> (adopted in 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of health services, WHO looks to improve "governance, financing, staffing and management" and the availability and quality of evidence and research to guide policy making. It also strives to "ensure improved access, quality and use of medical products and technologies".<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup> WHO - working with donor agencies and national governments - can improve their use of and their reporting about their use of research evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_support">Governance and support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Governance and support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The remaining two of WHO's thirteen identified policy areas relate to the role of WHO itself:<sup id="cite_ref-20123budget_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20123budget-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"to provide leadership, strengthen governance and foster partnership and collaboration with countries, the United Nations system, and other stakeholders in order to fulfill the mandate of WHO in advancing the global health agenda"; and</li>
<li>"to develop and sustain WHO as a flexible, learning organization, enabling it to carry out its mandate more efficiently and effectively".</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The WHO along with the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> constitute the core team responsible for administering the <a href="/wiki/International_Health_Partnership" title="International Health Partnership">International Health Partnership</a> (IHP+). The IHP+ is a group of partner governments, development agencies, civil society and others committed to improving the health of citizens in <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>. Partners work together to put international principles for <a href="/wiki/Aid_effectiveness" title="Aid effectiveness">aid effectiveness</a> and development cooperation into practice in the health sector.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The organization relies on contributions from renowned scientists and professionals to inform its work, such as the <a href="/wiki/WHO_Expert_Committee_on_Biological_Standardization" title="WHO Expert Committee on Biological Standardization">WHO Expert Committee on Biological Standardization</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/WHO_Expert_Committee_on_Leprosy" title="WHO Expert Committee on Leprosy">WHO Expert Committee on Leprosy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Interprofessional_education#WHO_Study_Group_on_Interprofessional_Education_.26_Collaborative_Practice" title="Interprofessional education">WHO Study Group on Interprofessional Education &amp; Collaborative Practice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO runs the Alliance for Health Policy and Systems Research, targeted at improving <a href="/wiki/Health_policy" title="Health policy">health policy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Health_system" title="Health system">systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO also aims to improve access to health research and literature in developing countries such as through the <a href="/wiki/HINARI" title="HINARI">HINARI</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health_education_and_action">Public health education and action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Public health education and action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Each year, the organization marks <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Day" title="World Health Day">World Health Day</a> and other observances focusing on a specific <a href="/wiki/Health_promotion" title="Health promotion">health promotion</a> topic. World Health Day falls on 7 April each year, timed to match the anniversary of WHO's founding. Recent themes have been <a href="/wiki/Vector_(epidemiology)" title="Vector (epidemiology)">vector-borne diseases</a> (2014), healthy ageing (2012) and <a href="/wiki/Drug_resistance" title="Drug resistance">drug resistance</a> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The other official global public health campaigns marked by WHO are <a href="/wiki/World_Tuberculosis_Day" title="World Tuberculosis Day">World Tuberculosis Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Immunization_Week" title="World Immunization Week">World Immunization Week</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Malaria_Day" title="World Malaria Day">World Malaria Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_No_Tobacco_Day" title="World No Tobacco Day">World No Tobacco Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Blood_Donor_Day" title="World Blood Donor Day">World Blood Donor Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Hepatitis_Day" title="World Hepatitis Day">World Hepatitis Day</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_AIDS_Day" title="World AIDS Day">World AIDS Day</a>.</p>
<p>As part of the United Nations, the World Health Organization supports work towards the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Of the eight Millennium Development Goals, three – reducing child mortality by two-thirds, to reduce maternal deaths by three-quarters, and to halt and begin to reduce the spread of HIV/AIDS – relate directly to WHO's scope; the other five inter-relate and have an impact on world health.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_handling_and_publications">Data handling and publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Data handling and publications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The World Health Organization works to provide the needed health and well-being evidence through a variety of data collection platforms, including the World Health Survey covering almost 400,000 respondents from 70 countries,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Study_on_Global_Ageing_and_Adult_Health" title="Study on Global Ageing and Adult Health">Study on Global Ageing and Adult Health</a></i> (SAGE) covering over 50,000 persons over 50 years old in 23 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The Country Health Intelligence Portal (CHIP), has also been developed to provide an access point to information about the health services that are available in different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The information gathered in this portal is utilized by the countries to set priorities for future strategies or plans, implement, monitor, and evaluate it.</p>
<p>The WHO has published various tools for measuring and monitoring the capacity of national <a href="/wiki/Health_system" title="Health system">health systems</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Health_Human_Resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Health Human Resources">health workforces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The Global Health Observatory (GHO) has been the WHO's main portal which provides access to data and analyses for key health themes by monitoring health situations around the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>WHO Assessment Instrument for Mental Health Systems</i> (WHO-AIMS), the <i>WHO Quality of Life Instrument</i> (WHOQOL), and the <i>Service Availability and Readiness Assessment</i> (SARA) provide guidance for data collection.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Collaborative efforts between WHO and other agencies, such as through the <a href="/wiki/Health_Metrics_Network" title="Health Metrics Network">Health Metrics Network</a>, also aim to provide sufficient high-quality information to assist governmental decision making.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> WHO promotes the development of capacities in member states to use and produce research that addresses their national needs, including through the <a href="/wiki/Evidence-Informed_Policy_Network" title="Evidence-Informed Policy Network">Evidence-Informed Policy Network</a> (EVIPNet).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The Pan American Health Organization (PAHO/AMRO) became the first region to develop and pass a policy on research for health approved in September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 December 2013, a new WHO database, known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=MiNDbank&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MiNDbank (page does not exist)">MiNDbank</a>, went online. The database was launched on <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Day" title="Human Rights Day">Human Rights Day</a>, and is part of WHO's QualityRights initiative, which aims to end human rights violations against people with mental health conditions. The new database presents a great deal of information about mental health, substance abuse, disability, human rights, and the different policies, strategies, laws, and service standards being implemented in different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-MiNDbank_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiNDbank-62">[62]</a></sup> It also contains important international documents and information. The database allows visitors to access the health information of WHO member states and other partners. Users can review policies, laws, and strategies and search for the best practices and success stories in the field of mental health.<sup id="cite_ref-MiNDbank_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MiNDbank-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The WHO regularly publishes a <i><a href="/wiki/World_Health_Report" title="World Health Report">World Health Report</a></i>, its leading publication, including an expert assessment of a specific <a href="/wiki/Global_health" title="Global health">global health</a> topic.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Other publications of WHO include the <i><a href="/wiki/Bulletin_of_the_World_Health_Organization" title="Bulletin of the World Health Organization">Bulletin of the World Health Organization</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_Health_Journal" title="Eastern Mediterranean Health Journal">Eastern Mediterranean Health Journal</a></i> (overseen by EMRO),<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> the <i><a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_for_Health" title="Human Resources for Health">Human Resources for Health</a></i> (published in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/BioMed_Central" title="BioMed Central">BioMed Central</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Journal_of_Public_Health" title="Pan American Journal of Public Health">Pan American Journal of Public Health</a></i> (overseen by PAHO/AMRO).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The World Health Organization is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Group" title="United Nations Development Group">United Nations Development Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png/220px-World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png/330px-World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png/440px-World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organization_membership_status_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Countries by World Health Organization membership status</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the WHO has 194 member states: all of them Member States of the United Nations except for the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-countries_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countries-69">[69]</a></sup> (A state becomes a full member of WHO by ratifying the treaty known as the Constitution of the World Health Organization.) As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it also had two associate members, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">Tokelau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Several other countries have been granted <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">observer status</a>. <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> is an observer as a "national liberation movement" recognised by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Arab_States" class="mw-redirect" title="League of Arab States">League of Arab States</a> under United Nations Resolution 3118. The <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> also attends as an observer, as does the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Order of Malta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-observerWHO_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observerWHO-71">[71]</a></sup> In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Taiwan</a> was invited under the name of "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Chinese Taipei</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO Member States appoint delegations to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a>, WHO's supreme decision-making body. All UN Member States are eligible for WHO membership, and, according to the WHO web site, "other countries may be admitted as members when their application has been approved by a simple majority vote of the World Health Assembly".<sup id="cite_ref-countries_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countries-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, the UN observer organizations <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a> have entered into "official relations" with WHO and are invited as observers. In the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a> they are seated alongside the other NGOs.<sup id="cite_ref-observerWHO_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-observerWHO-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assembly_and_Executive_Board">Assembly and Executive Board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Assembly and Executive Board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg/220px-World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg/330px-World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg/440px-World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organisation_building_south_face_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
WHO Headquarters in Geneva</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The World Health Assembly is the legislative and supreme body of WHO. Based in Geneva, it typically meets yearly in May. It appoints the Director-General every five years, and votes on matters of policy and finance of WHO, including the proposed budget. It also reviews reports of the Executive Board and decides whether there are areas of work requiring further examination. The Assembly elects 34 members, technically qualified in the field of health, to the Executive Board for three-year terms. The main functions of the Board are to carry out the decisions and policies of the Assembly, to advise it and to facilitate its work.<sup id="cite_ref-governance_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_offices">Regional offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Regional offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg/220px-World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg.png" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg/330px-World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg/440px-World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Health_Organisation_regional_offices.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Regional offices and regions of the WHO:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #1a80e6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Africa; HQ: <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Congo">Congo</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #7ae6ce; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Health_Organization" title="Pan American Health Organization">Americas</a>; HQ: Washington, DC, USA</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f2c50d; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Eastern <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Med.</a>; HQ: <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #15ea15; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Europe; HQ: <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #c018e1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;South East Asia; HQ: New Delhi, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #f20d0d; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Western Pacific; HQ: <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The regional divisions of WHO were created between 1949 and 1952, and are based on article 44 of WHO's constitution, which allowed the WHO to "establish a [single] regional organization to meet the special needs of [each defined] area". Many decisions are made at regional level, including important discussions over WHO's budget, and in deciding the members of the next assembly, which are designated by the regions.<sup id="cite_ref-burci53_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burci53-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each region has a Regional Committee, which generally meets once a year, normally in the autumn. Representatives attend from each member or associative member in each region, including those states that are not fully recognised. For example, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> attends meetings of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_Regional_office_of_World_Health_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Mediterranean Regional office of World Health Organization">Eastern Mediterranean Regional office</a>. Each region also has a regional office.<sup id="cite_ref-burci53_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burci53-74">[74]</a></sup> Each Regional Office is headed by a Regional Director, who is elected by the Regional Committee. The Board must approve such appointments, although as of 2004, it had never overruled the preference of a regional committee. The exact role of the board in the process has been a subject of debate, but the practical effect has always been small.<sup id="cite_ref-burci53_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burci53-74">[74]</a></sup> Since 1999, Regional Directors serve for a once-renewable five-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each Regional Committee of the WHO consists of all the Health Department heads, in all the governments of the countries that constitute the Region. Aside from electing the Regional Director, the Regional Committee is also in charge of setting the guidelines for the implementation, within the region, of the health and other policies adopted by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a>. The Regional Committee also serves as a progress review board for the actions of WHO within the Region.</p>
<p>The Regional Director is effectively the head of WHO for his or her Region. The RD manages and/or supervises a staff of health and other experts at the regional offices and in specialized centers. The RD is also the direct supervising authority—concomitantly with the WHO Director-General—of all the heads of WHO country offices, known as WHO Representatives, within the Region.</p>

<td>Eastern Mediterranean</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_Regional_office_of_World_Health_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Mediterranean Regional office of World Health Organization">Eastern Mediterranean Regional office</a> includes the countries of Africa that are not included in AFRO, as well as the countries of the Middle East, except for Israel. <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> is served by EMRO.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></td>
<td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.emro.who.int">EMRO</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Western Pacific</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>, Philippines.</td>
<td>WPRO covers all the Asian countries not served by SEARO and EMRO, and all the countries in Oceania. <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> is served by WPRO.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></td>
<td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wpro.who.int">WPRO</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The Americas</td>
<td>Washington D.C., USA.</td>
<td>Also known as the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Health_Organization" title="Pan American Health Organization">Pan American Health Organization</a> (PAHO), and covers the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The Regional Director is <a href="/wiki/Carissa_F._Etienne" title="Carissa F. Etienne">Carissa F. Etienne</a>.</td>
<td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paho.org">AMRO</a></td>
</tr>
</table>

<td colspan="2"><small>*Acting Director-General following the death of Lee Jong-wook while in office</small></td>
