</table>
<p>The head of the organization is the Director-General, elected by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-governance_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-governance-73">[73]</a></sup> The current Director-General is <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Chan" title="Margaret Chan">Margaret Chan</a>, who was first appointed on 9 November 2006<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and confirmed for a second term until the end of June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>WHO employs 8,500 people in 147 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> In support of the principle of a tobacco-free work environment the WHO does not recruit cigarette smokers.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The organization has previously instigated the <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_on_Tobacco_Control" class="mw-redirect" title="Framework Convention on Tobacco Control">Framework Convention on Tobacco Control</a> in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>The WHO operates "<a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization_Goodwill_Ambassador" title="World Health Organization Goodwill Ambassador">Goodwill Ambassadors</a>", members of the arts, sport or other fields of public life aimed at drawing attention to WHO's initiatives and projects. There are currently five Goodwill Ambassadors (<a href="/wiki/Jet_Li" title="Jet Li">Jet Li</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Brinker" title="Nancy Brinker">Nancy Brinker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peng_Liyuan" title="Peng Liyuan">Peng Liyuan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yohei_Sasakawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Yohei Sasakawa">Yohei Sasakawa</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Philharmonic_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Vienna Philharmonic Orchestra">Vienna Philharmonic Orchestra</a>) and a further ambassador associated with a partnership project (<a href="/wiki/Craig_David" title="Craig David">Craig David</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Country_and_liaison_offices">Country and liaison offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Country and liaison offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The World Health Organization operates 147 country offices in all its regions.<sup id="cite_ref-peopleandoffices_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peopleandoffices-89">[89]</a></sup> It also operates several liaison offices, including those with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, United Nations and a single office covering the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>. It also operates the <a href="/wiki/International_Agency_for_Research_on_Cancer" title="International Agency for Research on Cancer">International Agency for Research on Cancer</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, France, and the <a href="/wiki/WHO_Centre_for_Health_Development" title="WHO Centre for Health Development">WHO Centre for Health Development</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kobe" title="Kobe">Kobe</a>, Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Additional offices include those in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>; the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a>; the US-Mexico Border Field Office in <a href="/wiki/El_Paso" class="mw-redirect" title="El Paso">El Paso</a>; the Office of the Caribbean Program Coordination in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>; and Northern Micronesia office.<sup id="cite_ref-detailedinformation_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detailedinformation-91">[91]</a></sup> There will generally be one WHO country office in the capital, occasionally accompanied by satellite-offices in the provinces or sub-regions of the country in question.</p>
<p>The country office is headed by a WHO Representative (WR). As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the only WHO Representative outside Europe to be a national of that country was for the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect" title="Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">Libyan Arab Jamahiriya</a> ("Libya"); all other staff were international. Those in the Region for the Americas, they are referred to as PAHO/WHO Representatives. In Europe, WHO Representatives also serve as Head of Country Office, and are nationals with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>; there are also Heads of Country Office in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-detailedinformation_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detailedinformation-91">[91]</a></sup> The WR is member of the <a href="/wiki/UN_system" class="mw-redirect" title="UN system">UN system</a> country team which is coordinated by the UN System <a href="/wiki/Resident_Coordinator" title="Resident Coordinator">Resident Coordinator</a>.</p>
<p>The country office consists of the WR, and several health and other experts, both foreign and local, as well as the necessary support staff.<sup id="cite_ref-peopleandoffices_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peopleandoffices-89">[89]</a></sup> The main functions of WHO country offices include being the primary adviser of that country's government in matters of health and pharmaceutical policies.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financing_and_partnerships">Financing and partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Financing and partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WHO is financed by contributions from member states and outside donors. As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the largest annual assessed contributions from member states came from the United States ($110&#160;million), Japan ($58&#160;million), Germany ($37&#160;million), United Kingdom ($31&#160;million) and France ($31&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The combined 2012–2013 budget has proposed a total expenditure of $3,959&#160;million, of which $944&#160;million (24%) will come from assessed contributions. This represented a significant fall in outlay compared to the previous 2009–2010 budget, adjusting to take account of previous underspends. Assessed contributions were kept the same. Voluntary contributions will account for $3,015&#160;million (76%), of which $800&#160;million is regarded as highly or moderately flexible funding, with the remainder tied to particular programmes or objectives.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In recent years, the WHO's work has involved increasing collaboration with external bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> As of 2002<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 473 <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> (NGO) had some form of partnership with WHO. There were 189 partnerships with international NGOs in formal "official relations" – the rest being considered informal in character.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Partners include the <a href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IAEA_.E2.80.93_Agreement_WHA_12.E2.80.9340">IAEA – Agreement WHA 12–40</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: IAEA – Agreement WHA 12–40">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexei_Yablokov,_Rosa_Goncharova,_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg/220px-Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg/330px-Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg/440px-Alexei_Yablokov%2C_Rosa_Goncharova%2C_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexei_Yablokov,_Rosa_Goncharova,_Vassili_Nesterenko.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alexey_Yablokov" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexey Yablokov">Alexey Yablokov</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Vassili_Nesterenko" title="Vassili Nesterenko">Vassili Nesterenko</a> (farthest right) protesting in front of the World Health Organization headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, Switzerland in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devant_OMS_5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Devant_OMS_5.jpg/220px-Devant_OMS_5.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Devant_OMS_5.jpg/330px-Devant_OMS_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Devant_OMS_5.jpg/440px-Devant_OMS_5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2983" data-file-height="2383" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devant_OMS_5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Demonstration on <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl disaster</a> day near WHO in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1959, the WHO signed Agreement WHA 12–40 with the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (IAEA). The agreement states that the WHO recognises the IAEA as having responsibility for peaceful nuclear energy without prejudice to the roles of the WHO of promoting health. However, the following paragraph adds that "whenever either organization proposes to initiate a programme or activity on a subject in which the other organization has or may have a substantial interest, the first party shall consult the other with a view to adjusting the matter by mutual agreement".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The nature of this statement has led some pressure groups and activists (including <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Europe_for_a_Common_Future" title="Women in Europe for a Common Future">Women in Europe for a Common Future</a>) to believe that the WHO is restricted in its ability to investigate the <a href="/wiki/Acute_radiation_syndrome" title="Acute radiation syndrome">effects on human health of radiation</a> caused by the use of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> and the continuing effects of <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_nuclear_disasters_and_radioactive_incidents" title="Lists of nuclear disasters and radioactive incidents">nuclear disasters</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_nuclear_disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Fukushima nuclear disaster">Fukushima</a>. They believe WHO must regain what they see as "independence".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholic_Church_and_AIDS">Roman Catholic Church and AIDS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Roman Catholic Church and AIDS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church_and_AIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church and AIDS">Roman Catholic Church and AIDS</a></div>
<p>In 2003, the WHO denounced the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a>'s health department's opposition to the use of <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condoms</a>, saying: "These incorrect statements about condoms and HIV are dangerous when we are facing a global pandemic which has already killed more than 20&#160;million people, and currently affects at least 42&#160;million."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Catholic Church remains opposed to increasing the use of contraception to combat HIV/AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> At the time, the World Health Assembly President, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>'s Health Minister <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Ramsammy" title="Leslie Ramsammy">Leslie Ramsammy</a>, condemned <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict's</a> opposition to contraception, saying he was trying to "create confusion" and "impede" proven strategies in the battle against the disease.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intermittent_preventive_therapy">Intermittent preventive therapy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Intermittent preventive therapy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The aggressive support of the <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation</a> for <a href="/wiki/Intermittent_preventive_therapy" title="Intermittent preventive therapy">intermittent preventive therapy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> triggered a memo from the former WHO malaria chief Akira Kochi.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diet_and_sugar_intake">Diet and sugar intake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Diet and sugar intake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some of the research undertaken or supported by WHO to determine how people's lifestyles and environments are influencing whether they live in better or worse health can be controversial, as illustrated by a 2003 joint WHO/FAO report on nutrition and the prevention of chronic <a href="/wiki/Non-communicable_disease" title="Non-communicable disease">non-communicable disease</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> which recommended that sugar should form no more than 10% of a <a href="/wiki/Healthy_diet" title="Healthy diet">healthy diet</a>. The report led to lobbying by the sugar industry against the recommendation, to which the WHO/FAO responded by including in the report this statement: "The Consultation recognized that a population goal for free sugars of less than 10% of total energy is controversial". It also stood by its recommendation based upon its own analysis of scientific studies.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2014, WHO reduced recommended sugar levels by half and said that sugar should make up no more than 5% of a healthy diet.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_swine_flu_pandemic">2009 swine flu pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2009 swine flu pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic" title="2009 flu pandemic">2009 flu pandemic</a></div>
<p>In 2007, the WHO organized work on pandemic <a href="/wiki/Influenza_vaccine" title="Influenza vaccine">influenza vaccine</a> development through <a href="/wiki/Clinical_trial" title="Clinical trial">clinical trials</a> in collaboration with many experts. A pandemic involving the <a href="/wiki/Pandemic_H1N1/09_virus" title="Pandemic H1N1/09 virus">H1N1 influenza virus</a> was declared by Director-General <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Chan" title="Margaret Chan">Margaret Chan</a> in April 2009.</p>
<p>By the post-pandemic period critics claimed the WHO had exaggerated the danger, spreading "fear and confusion" rather than "immediate information".<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Industry experts countered that the 2009 pandemic had led to "unprecedented collaboration between global health authorities, scientists and manufacturers, resulting in the most comprehensive pandemic response ever undertaken, with a number of vaccines approved for use three months after the pandemic declaration. This response was only possible because of the extensive preparations undertaken in during the last decade".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013-16_Ebola_outbreak_and_reform_efforts">2013-16 Ebola outbreak and reform efforts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 2013-16 Ebola outbreak and reform efforts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ebola_outbreak" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Ebola outbreak">2014 Ebola outbreak</a> in West Africa, the organization was heavily criticized for its bureaucracy, insufficient financing, regional structure, and staffing profile.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>An internal WHO report on the Ebola response pointed to underfunding and lack of "core capacity" in health systems in developing countries as the primary weaknesses of the existing system. At the annual World Health Assembly in 2015, Director General Margaret Chan announced a $100 million Contingency Fund for rapid response to future emergencies,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> of which it had received $26.9 million by April 2016 (for 2017 disbursement). WHO has budgeted an additional $494 million for its Health Emergencies Programme in 2016-17, for which it had received $140 million by April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The program was aimed at rebuilding WHO capacity for direct action, which critics said had been lost due to budget cuts in the previous decade that had left the organization in an advisory role dependent on member states for on-the-ground activities. In comparison, billions of dollars have been spent by developed countries on the 2013-16 Ebola epidemic and 2015-16 Zika epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FCTC_implementation_database">FCTC implementation database</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: FCTC implementation database">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The WHO has a Framework Convention on Tobacco implementation database which is one of the only mechanisms to help enforce compliance with the FCTC.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> However, there has been reports of numerous discrepancies between it and national implementation reports on which it was built. As researchers Hoffman and Rizvi report "As of July 4, 2012, 361 (32·7%) of 1104 countries' responses were misreported: 33 (3·0%) were clear errors (eg, database indicated “yes” when report indicated “no”), 270 (24·5%) were missing despite countries having submitted responses, and 58 (5·3%) were, in our opinion, misinterpreted by WHO staff".<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_headquarters">World headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Health_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: World headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The seat of the organization is in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, Switzerland. It was dedicated and opened in 1966.</p>
